## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration (dv_dt) is determined by position x, velocity v, and possibly time t. The relationship encodes the equation of motion including nonlinear restoring forces, possible damping, and possible external driving.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (undriven): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (linear + periodic driving)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing equation)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinearity)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (position-dependent stiffness)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Combined quadratic-cubic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (general polynomial restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping with driving: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v * x**2 + c4 * cos(c5 * t)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) indicate symmetric potential wells; even powers (x**2) indicate asymmetric potentials
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v represent linear damping/anti-damping; terms like (1 - c*x**2)*v indicate amplitude-dependent damping (limit cycles)
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicates external periodic driving forces
- Cubic position terms x**3 with same sign as linear term x indicate hardening spring; opposite sign indicates softening spring (Duffing classification)
- Cross terms like x**2 * v or x * v suggest nonlinear dissipation mechanisms coupling position and velocity
- Pure position-dependent acceleration (no v or t terms) implies a conservative system derivable from a potential energy function
- Sinusoidal functions of position sin(c*x) suggest rotational/pendulum-type dynamics rather than polynomial springs
- Products of trigonometric functions of time with position (x*cos(c*t)) indicate parametric excitation rather than direct forcing
